  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f8fd0cbb-4fc9-47ea-9b92-026056cc870c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3452190291" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14058695115584254073">Oh man this is fantastic. How had I not read it before?! I rewatched the movie last night (for like the 10th time) and reading it made me want to just have it on all the time. It’s such a great VIBE. I’m going to have to read the rest of the series for sure!!!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1751675829" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1751675829" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1751675829?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1751675829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7780194252791160970"><b>
  <u>Game on!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><i>This is the first book (in a series of six) of “Scott Pilgrim” saga.</i><br/><br/><br/><u>Creative Team:</u><br/><br/>Creator, writer and illustrator: Bryan Lee O’Malley <br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>AM I DREAMING?</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Um… am I dreaming? -- -- I’ll leave you alone forever now.</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Thanks.</i>
</b><br/><br/>My first contact with <i>Scott Pilgrim</i>’s world was through the movie adaptation, that I wouldn’t watch (at least not so soon as I did) if Mary Elizabeth Winstead (which I love) wouldn’t be in the cast. <br/><br/>And I would lost a lot! Since that movie rules!<br/><br/>So bizarre, cleve</span>
  <span id="freeText7780194252791160970" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Game on!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><i>This is the first book (in a series of six) of “Scott Pilgrim” saga.</i><br /><br /><br /><u>Creative Team:</u><br /><br />Creator, writer and illustrator: Bryan Lee O’Malley <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>AM I DREAMING?</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Um… am I dreaming? -- -- I’ll leave you alone forever now.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Thanks.</i>
</b><br /><br />My first contact with <i>Scott Pilgrim</i>’s world was through the movie adaptation, that I wouldn’t watch (at least not so soon as I did) if Mary Elizabeth Winstead (which I love) wouldn’t be in the cast. <br /><br />And I would lost a lot! Since that movie rules!<br /><br />So bizarre, clever, exciting and funny! Am I dreaming? This movie was just right for me!<br /><br />I was watching it again last week (I have it in DVD and Bluray, and yes I am keeping both editions since the DVD has a magenta background in its cover, and the Bluray has a blue background in its cover, and if you know the most basic things about Ramona Flowers (Mary Elizabeth Winstead’s character) you well know that this is just wonderful and yes, I’d need a future format edition in a green background, dang it!).<br /><br />So, I was watching once again the movie, and again I was thinking that I should read the original Canadian mangas (or are they comics? Whatever, dudes) and…<br /><br />…in the following weekend I went to the XVII International Book Fair (a yearly book event in my country (Costa Rica)) and in a stand, there was a set with all 6 books (actually there were two sets, but it sounds more epic saying that there was just one set!) (and even with a special discount due the fair), am I dreaming? There it was just the right set of books waiting for me…<br /><br />…<b>take my money and give me that set!!!</b><br /><br />And finally I am reading the epic saga. <br /><br />By the way, I am sure, some of you, are wondering, and the movie adaptation covers the six books in the series, so nope, it’s not like the first book is the movie, and you’d read other adventures in the other five books. Nope. The six books in the Canadian manga series are what you get in the movie (of course, you may expect some deeper detailing here and there, and different approaches to the scenes).<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>PILGRIM’S PATH</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>What kind of tea do you want?</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>There’s more than one kind of tea?</i>
</b><br /><br />The world of Scott Pilgrim (story’s main character) is a wacky one where silly things like physics’ laws aren’t quite existing so you can have the maximum level of fun there…<br /><br />…So, this is a looney world when dream state highways can be a casual talk, 23-years old boys don’t know the basics of internet and e-mail (trust me, that’s not normal), and losing fighting dudes can turn into coins…<br /><br />…yes, you heard me. Deal it. Chew it. Move on. <br /><br />Scott Pilgrim is a 23 years old dude, he lives in Toronto, Canada, he’s between jobs and current bass player in a band, the Sex Bob-Omb (desperately trying to get a discographic contract). Scott has a roommate, Wallace Wells, gay, and Scott’s voice of conscience. Scott’s younger sister is Stacey Pilgrim and she’s the other voice of conscience for Scott. Yep. You betcha that Scott needs all voices of conscience available.<br /><br />By the way, the Sex Bob-Omb are: Stephen Stills (the talent, guitar player and leader of the band), Kim Pine (drums) and (Young) Neil Nordegraf (biggest Sex Bob-Omb’s fan (until Knives Chau (keep reading) comes in)).<br /><br />And at the beginning of the story, Scott just started to date a high schooler: Knives Chau, 17 years old, Chinese and in a Catholic school (yes, with uniform), so yeah, Scott has no shame, but technically that’s not the problem, nope, life gets really complicated when Scott meets…<br /><br />…<b>Ramona Flowers</b>.<br /><br />Ramona Flowers, none disclosured age (in this first book) but clearly twenty-something, American, recently she moved to Canada, and she’s the only delivery girl in Toronto’s downtown area for Amazon.ca. She wears cool outfits and has magenta colored hair (later she’d changing the color to blue and later to green) and she travels in rollerblades. Gorgeous. Smart. Cool. Perfect. (It helps that beyond the basic manga appearance, I keep thinking in Mary Elizabeth Winstead’s version). Oh, and she’s the best living blanket ever in the history of mangas (and movies by the way). Oooh, yeah.<br /><br />But if you think that complications are due Scott is so lame to start dating Ramona without officially breaking up with Knives, nope, that’s not it…<br /><br />…Oh, don’t get me wrong, double dating (especially if one of them is an underage girl) is still a very douchebag thing to do (I like Scott, but men shouldn’t do that to women (and viceversa)), but, nope, that’s not the new complication factor introduced in Scott Pilgrim’s life…<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>ENTER THE LEAGUE</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>You dated seven evil dudes?</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Not all at once!</i>
</b><br /><br />Everybody has a past. It’s impossible that you meet new people in your life without being certain that that new people have a past.<br /><br />Scott has a past (that we all get to know in the following books in the series).<br /><br />And Ramona has a past too.<br /><br />The problem with Ramona’s past is that it (literally) follows her and interferes with any chance for her of newer romantic relationships.<br /><br />The League of Seven Evil Ex-boyfriends is a non-profit organization, homebased in America (but currently expanding to Canadian territory) with a single marketing goal: To destroy any newer boyfriend in Ramona Flowers’ life.<br /><br />Oh, and if you think that that was bad enough, nope, that’s not the worst part…<br /><br />…wait for it…<br /><br />…keep waiting a little longer…<br /><br />…the seven members of the League of Seven Evil Ex-boyfriends have super powers…<br /><br />…yes, you heard (well, read actually) right…<br /><br />…super powers!<br /><br />I told you that physics’ laws left the building for good!<br /><br />In this first book, you’ll meet Matthew Pattel, with mystical powers and decided to fight against Scott Pilgrim. But, even for an evil ex-boyfriend, Pattel is quite fair and he sent two letters, one per e-mail and one per snail mail (yes, people still do that! That’s not something up in this wacky world), too bad that Scott found boring to read anything, even if they’re death threat warnings! <br /><br />So…<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Open your eyes up… Maybe you’ll see…</i>
</b> Scott Pilgrim’s world!!!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7780194252791160970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1659332459" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1659332459" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1659332459?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1659332459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7806276603204529182"><b>DNF at page 54</b>.<br/><br/><a href='https://bookspoils.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465121821ra/19316418.gif' width='500' height='275' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>(This was exactly what I was feeling while reading <b>Scott Pilgrim's Precious Little Life</b>.)<br/><br/>I actually tried watching the movie a while back, but it made me really, really uncomfortable. And the same happened while reading the graphic novel. <br/><br/>I wanted to read it because I really liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1658663966?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seconds</a>, but I guess I somehow forgot that the movie was based off of a graphic novel. And I hadn’t made the connection between the two until I started reading and feeling really (and I mean really) </span>
  <span id="freeText7806276603204529182" style="display:none"><b>DNF at page 54</b>.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465121821ra/19316418.gif" width="500" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(This was exactly what I was feeling while reading <b>Scott Pilgrim's Precious Little Life</b>.)<br><br>I actually tried watching the movie a while back, but it made me really, really uncomfortable. And the same happened while reading the graphic novel. <br><br>I wanted to read it because I really liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1658663966?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Seconds</a>, but I guess I somehow forgot that the movie was based off of a graphic novel. And I hadn’t made the connection between the two until I started reading and feeling really (and I mean really) uneasy. <br><br>I was uncomfortable with the fact that Scott Pilgrim, a 23 year old, was dating a high schooler. I just personally can’t stand by that (even if he is <u>incredibly</u> immature).<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465121821ra/19316419.gif" width="500" height="265" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I mean, just looking at him waiting for Knives to finish her day at school made me want to throw up a little.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465121821i/19316420._SY540_.png" width="433" height="690" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Never has a book made me this physically uncomfortable. <b>Wow</b>.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465121821i/19316421.png" width="450" height="340" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>I was so close to giving up after this section and I kept thinking, "I don’t hate myself this much, I can put it down."<br><br>Maybe it’s a personal thing, but I just can’t get over how uncomfortable my reading experience was.<br><br>Example number 20 of Scott's immaturity:<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465121821i/19316422.png" width="440" height="326" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br>Really, ‘no girls allowed’??? How old are you???<br><br>I was holding on for it to get better, but then stuff like this gets thrown in, and I’m just not about that life.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465121821i/19316423.png" width="450" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>There wasn't even <b>one</b> likeable character. ONE.<br><br>I’m truly perplexed at how different <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1658663966?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Seconds</a> is compared to this catastrophe. Even the humor is on extremely different levels. I just don't get how the same person wrote this.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465121821ra/19316424.gif" width="320" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>Scott Pilgrim's Precious Little Life</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. <div id="review_24566782" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24566782" />
    <a title="Traci Haley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/404169-traci-haley"><img alt="Traci Haley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500923058p2/404169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24566782?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Traci Haley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Traci Haley" href="/user/show/404169-traci-haley">Traci Haley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/404169-traci-haley?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/404169-traci-haley?shelf=2008">2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24566782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5951539505693056742">I debated what to rate this graphic novel. On the one hand, the characters are thoroughly unlikable. Scott Pilgrim is a vapid, useless lump of a man who is dating a high schooler because that's the level of his maturity/emotional intelligence. Ramona Flowers is standoffish and rude because it makes her look "cool". The only redeeming character was Wallace, the gay roommate. On the other hand, once introductions got over, during the last scene of the book (the concert and Scott's fight with the f</span>
  <span id="freeText5951539505693056742" style="display:none">I debated what to rate this graphic novel. On the one hand, the characters are thoroughly unlikable. Scott Pilgrim is a vapid, useless lump of a man who is dating a high schooler because that's the level of his maturity/emotional intelligence. Ramona Flowers is standoffish and rude because it makes her look "cool". The only redeeming character was Wallace, the gay roommate. On the other hand, once introductions got over, during the last scene of the book (the concert and Scott's fight with the first evil ex-boyfriend) I really started to like this quirky, little story. The art is definitely not a factor -- the drawings are little more than scribbles on the page and I daresay I could probably do just as well. I will probably continue reading to find out what happens. And when the movie comes out, I'll probably see it... I now believe that Michael Cera was brilliant casting for Scott Pilgrim's character, because I hate Michael Cera with a passion, too. Perhaps one of Ramona's evil ex boyfriends will triumph? One can only hope.<br /><br />Edited to add: Three years later, I decided to revisit this review, as it has occasionally garnered some comments from people annoyed at my audacity to hold an opinion. I'm not going to change my rating because my opinion stands firm. I really *didn't* care greatly for the first volume of Scott Pilgrim. But I also went on to read all the subsequent volumes...and fell in love with the series, the characters (maybe not Scott... I still kind of dislike him...), and yes, even the artwork. I even enjoyed the movie (except for Michael Cera... I still hate him, too). So anyone thinking about starting this series? DO... and keep going, even if the first one doesn't dazzle you like it didn't dazzle me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5951539505693056742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_385879480" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/385879480" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/385879480?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781620100004" href="/book/show/14080417-scott-pilgrim-volume-1">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer385879480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11122678028741978787">“Scott Pilgrim is dating a high schooler!” - so begins one of the finest comics sagas of all time. <br/><br/>I’ve read Bryan Lee O’Malley’s Scott Pilgrim before, seen the (extremely faithful) Edgar Wright movie adaptation, and have just re-read it (this time in colour), and the comic still blows me away with its quality. Reading the same story the third time around and it’s not boring in the least. It even somehow feels fresh despite having been published in 2004! <br/><br/>On paper the story seems like no great sh</span>
  <span id="freeText11122678028741978787" style="display:none">“Scott Pilgrim is dating a high schooler!” - so begins one of the finest comics sagas of all time. <br /><br />I’ve read Bryan Lee O’Malley’s Scott Pilgrim before, seen the (extremely faithful) Edgar Wright movie adaptation, and have just re-read it (this time in colour), and the comic still blows me away with its quality. Reading the same story the third time around and it’s not boring in the least. It even somehow feels fresh despite having been published in 2004! <br /><br />On paper the story seems like no great shakes: 23 year old Scott is dating 17 year old Knives Chau, the aforementioned high schooler, (nothing funny, just holding hands), and then he meets Ramona Flowers, his literal dream girl whom he falls hard for. Just one catch: he’s gotta fight her 7 evil exes. And of course break up with poor unsuspecting Knives! <br /><br />It’s comedy romance mixed in with a Shonen Jump-style fight manga but the comic transcends the sum of its parts. O’Malley’s dialogue perfectly captures how young people in their late teens/early twenties talk albeit making them all very entertaining conversationalists. I’m sure it helped that he was in his early twenties when he wrote/drew this, but even then there’s a skill here with the writing and art that belies his (then) age. <br /><br />There’s very witty and warm-hearted humour that utilises the visual comics format well too - adding captions in a scene to emphasise how poor Scott is when in his and Wallace’s flat. The script is funny and fun and real and fantastical all at the same time - brilliant! Their names don’t bother me, nor the fact that the characters are all hipsters, that’s how good this comic is! <br /><br />It’s hard to describe how little seems to happen and yet it feels like so much is happening. The opening sequence is: 1) Scott and his friends in the kitchen talking, 2) Scott and Knives’ (intentionally) mundane meet-cute, 3) Wallace Wells (Scott’s gay flatmate) is introduced, 4) Scott introduces Knives to his band Sex Bob-Omb and they play a song. That’s it. Hardly anything really and YET - there’s so much energy, vibrancy, and urgency in these pages that’s indicative of the rest of the book (and series). It crackles with originality. <br /><br />O’Malley creates great characters and a helluva good story - Scott proving his love for Ramona in a way suited to his character and exciting to read too - but more than that, he captures the experience of being young and in love. That’s special. That’s something I’ve yet to come across in any other comic and that’s how you know you’re in the presence of a truly unique and obscenely talented voice. <br /><br />There’s not a single thing I could say I dislike about this book. Every scene brings it - not an ounce of fat is there to be found here! There are so many great moments, from Scott stalking Ramona at the party, to their first kiss, the battle of the bands against Crash and the Boys, the first evil ex, Matthew Patel, and their epic, synchronised fight. Ramona talking about using a shortcut through Scott’s mind to explain why he’s been dreaming about her is utterly bizarre but also fit perfectly into the tone of the book. <br /><br />O’Malley tosses in an occasional pop culture reference but it never overwhelms the story (Ernest Cline, take note!). Nathan Fairbairn’s colours are nice but the story was just as powerful in the original black and white so whichever version you read, the comic is still awesome. <br /><br />There are other creators who excel in both roles of writer and artist and have created startlingly original works - Frank Miller’s Sin City, David Lapham’s Stray Bullets, Eric Powell’s The Goon, Jeff Smith’s Bone, Akira Toriyama’s Dragon Ball, and Gilbert Hernandez’s Palomar stories - and Bryan Lee O’Malley’s Scott Pilgrim easily joins these elite ranks. <br /><br />Scott Pilgrim is about as flawless a comic as I can recommend to anyone. Whether you read comics or don’t, it’s absolutely worth reading. Scott Pilgrim’s Precious Little Life doesn’t age and wins over everyone who reads it - an instant classic and one of the best examples of the comics art form!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11122678028741978787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_668178421" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/668178421" />
    <a title="B Schrodinger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5448792-b-schrodinger"><img alt="B Schrodinger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572325701p2/5448792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/668178421?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B Schrodinger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B Schrodinger" href="/user/show/5448792-b-schrodinger">B Schrodinger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer668178421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17806679135144549960">Am I too old to like <i>Scott Pilgrim</i>?<br/><br/>I just don't care for a main character who is in his twenties, has no job, sleeps (the zzzzzzzz kind) with his roomate, dates a high school girl and cheats on her with a kinda cool delivery girl.<br/><br/>How is this guy attractive to women at all?<br/><br/>Back in my day...<br/><br/>This graphic novel made me feel old.<br/><br/><b>Scott Pilgrim is a bit of a dick</b> and it is hard to cheer for him when he is fighting his girlfriends ex boyfriends. I think the only way the author manages to make us on his </span>
  <span id="freeText17806679135144549960" style="display:none">Am I too old to like <i>Scott Pilgrim</i>?<br /><br />I just don't care for a main character who is in his twenties, has no job, sleeps (the zzzzzzzz kind) with his roomate, dates a high school girl and cheats on her with a kinda cool delivery girl.<br /><br />How is this guy attractive to women at all?<br /><br />Back in my day...<br /><br />This graphic novel made me feel old.<br /><br /><b>Scott Pilgrim is a bit of a dick</b> and it is hard to cheer for him when he is fighting his girlfriends ex boyfriends. I think the only way the author manages to make us on his side is to make the ex boyfriends even more of a tool.<br /><br />I guess I read this (probably a few years after the hype) to see what the kids are all talking about. <br /><br />But it isn't all bad and does deserve the 2-star "it was OK" rating. Good to read when you are tired and can't think.</span>

<div id="review_387656012" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/387656012" />
    <a title="Meredith Holley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley"><img alt="Meredith Holley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548641865p2/1302775.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/387656012?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith Holley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith Holley" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley">Meredith Holley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781620100004" href="/book/show/14080417-scott-pilgrim-volume-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=good-beach-reads">good-beach-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer387656012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2754535621309251349"><i>Scott Pilgrim</i> is so how I see the world. I’m sure it’s because of the years of doing almost nothing but playing Mario Bros in my childhood, but the levels and energy bars and coins, etc. as applied to mundane life things are so perfect to me. Also, the characters. Oh, the characters. Scott Pilgrim is such a rad character because he is so douchey, but still somewhat sympathetic, and everyone spends the whole story pointing out his doucheyness. I just really love a story that calls a douche a douc</span>
  <span id="freeText2754535621309251349" style="display:none"><i>Scott Pilgrim</i> is so how I see the world. I’m sure it’s because of the years of doing almost nothing but playing Mario Bros in my childhood, but the levels and energy bars and coins, etc. as applied to mundane life things are so perfect to me. Also, the characters. Oh, the characters. Scott Pilgrim is such a rad character because he is so douchey, but still somewhat sympathetic, and everyone spends the whole story pointing out his doucheyness. I just really love a story that calls a douche a douche.<br><br>This volume only gets so far as Scott fighting Ramona’s first evil ex. Scott is a little more boyish in this and a little less emo than Michael Cera, and I think both versions are pretty fun. For the most part, the movie follows this volume exactly, though the movie adds a few things that I think are hilarious – like Scott and Knives at the arcade, Scott’s story about Pac Man, and the way Scott describes Ramona’s hair. Maybe the arcade stuff happens later, but I could see how that would be easier to pull off on film than in a graphic novel.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386996i/746739._SX540_.gif" width="550" height="360" alt="the scene where scott describes ramona’s hair, but in the graphic novel he just uses his fingers, rather than drawing it" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’ve been reading a lot of graphic novels lately, mostly because people have given me a lot of them for some reason. This is one of my favorites because I think it is so clever. I don’t know if I would like it as much if I hadn’t seen the movie, but it’s hard to say. I think one of the things that I find sort of subtly hilarious in this story is how these insane male wish-fulfillment dreams will get fulfilled in the story, and Scott only reacts in a somewhat douchey way, but nobody freaks out. Like, battle of the bands is literally a Street Fighter-style cage match in which the music turns into monsters that fight each other, and Scott returns to the old, “Well, I knew I rocked, but I was not aware that we rocked collectively,” attitude. So brilliant. Is this because I have a little brother? And Scott reminds me of my little brother? Is that why I think this is so funny? Because all of Scott's conversations with his sister are so hilarious to me.<br><br>Digression: I saw the movie two or three times in the theater. One of the times was when I dragged my brother to see it, and he fully appreciated its genius, as I knew he would. Both (all?) times I saw it, the theater showed a preview for that movie <i>Devil</i>, and as the preview was showing people (including me) were like, "WTH??? What is this movie about? Oh my god, this looks so ridiculous," and then it would show M. NIGHT SHYAMALAN across the screen, and the whole theater would go, "Ohhhhhhhahahahaha!" American zeitgeist.<br><br>I don’t really think graphic novels are my thing. Maybe Persepolis is my thing, but in general I find them kind of boring. This wasn’t boring, but I don’t know if that was in large part because I knew what jokes were coming up. <br><br>I love Kim a lot. I must watch this movie again soon.<br>_______________________<br>I received a copy of this from Netgalley.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2754535621309251349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1302161510" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1302161510" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1302161510?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1302161510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2891214213178398710">This wasn't so bad, but that cover sucks.<br/><br/>I'm not that fond of reading contemporary novels, and it's no different with graphic novels. This had a simple plot, and nothing made it amazing for me. The artwork was decent, but I've seen way better. People have been recommending this everywhere, so I decided to finally give it a try. It's honestly not that bad, it would appeal more to the contemporary readers. I'm still interested to continue on with the series though. There's this mysterious thing ab</span>
  <span id="freeText2891214213178398710" style="display:none">This wasn't so bad, but that cover sucks.<br /><br />I'm not that fond of reading contemporary novels, and it's no different with graphic novels. This had a simple plot, and nothing made it amazing for me. The artwork was decent, but I've seen way better. People have been recommending this everywhere, so I decided to finally give it a try. It's honestly not that bad, it would appeal more to the contemporary readers. I'm still interested to continue on with the series though. There's this mysterious thing about a certain character which I'm not going to name to avoid possible spoilers.<br /><br />3/5 stars. Not something I would recommend normally, but go ahead and give it a try. You'll most probably enjoy this more than I did.</span>

<div id="review_114791991" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114791991" />
    <a title="J.G. Keely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84023-j-g-keely"><img alt="J.G. Keely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1274333636p2/84023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114791991?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.G. Keely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.G. Keely" href="/user/show/84023-j-g-keely">J.G. Keely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114791991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer926929286883501851">After the slow trudge through Shelley's 'The Last Man', I decided to switch to some lighter fare. It's about time I got back to my comic book to-read pile, anyways. So I pulled out Scott Pilgrim.<br/><br/>I've heard a lot about the book in comic book circles, and it's been overwhelmingly positive. Despite this, I've been somewhat wary of the 'trendy hipster' label it's been saddled with, but that gets thrown around too much, and I figured beyond the trendy elements, I'd get snatched up by something deeper</span>
  <span id="freeText926929286883501851" style="display:none">After the slow trudge through Shelley's 'The Last Man', I decided to switch to some lighter fare. It's about time I got back to my comic book to-read pile, anyways. So I pulled out Scott Pilgrim.<br /><br />I've heard a lot about the book in comic book circles, and it's been overwhelmingly positive. Despite this, I've been somewhat wary of the 'trendy hipster' label it's been saddled with, but that gets thrown around too much, and I figured beyond the trendy elements, I'd get snatched up by something deeper in the story or characterization, something to intrigue and beguile.<br /><br />So far, no such luck. It's reminiscent of 'Nick and Nora's Infinite Playlist', a movie I tired of about halfway through. Both of them are trying to be cutesy, quirky, ironic, and referential, but it's all very deliberate. I never felt there was a quick, complex mind at the helm, and with modern, referential humor, it's all about the delivery and the originality.<br /><br />Perhaps by this point, that type of humor has simply become structured and predictable, entering the mainstream and losing it's punch, like Jerry Seinfeld talking about airline food. Both Nick and Nora's and Scott Pilgrim were by-the-book quirky.<br /><br />Both also had somewhat unsettling homophobic overtones, playing off gay characters and same-sex romance for jokes. It's nice to have more openly gay characters in YA media, but not as thin, walking punchlines. It was much worse in 'Infinite Playlist', but there was still a persistent undercurrent of homosocial discomfort.<br /><br />The book was also very reminiscent of FLCL, from the mysterious, begoggled, badass delivery girl arriving to complicate the (sex) life of our oblivious jerk protagonist to the naive, sweet girl caught up in it all. Then the overt homages to manga and videogames start to trickle in, infesting the seemingly normal world of the comic with magic, fights, and all the rest.<br /><br />Yet unlike FLCL, this was not a rollicking, take-no-prisoners, psychedelic reimagining of a genre, it was just a dull story about annoying people occasionally perked up by in-joke fight scenes. The musical obsession was another shared thread, right down to the same characteristic Rickenbacker. It's not quite a parody, not quite an homage, and by refusing to take a stand, ends up with little to stand on.<br /><br />Then again, when "do you remember that family guy bit . . ." passes for a joke and "do you remember NES? Me too!" passes for a story, you can't expect much from the writing.<br /><br />The characters were the sort of dull, naive, self-absorbed people that I spent high school and college avoiding, right down to the fratboy favorite <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Poster-Print-Tanya-Chalkin-23x35/dp/B000EJQSH6" rel="nofollow noopener">lipstick lesbian poster</a> on the wall and an undying reverence for whatever bands Pitchfork told you to listen to this week. They're the sorts of people who would gush "my tastes are eclectic" followed by "music is my lifesblood" without a hint of irony. <br /><br />Scott himself is a mess, and yet without being either sympathetic or complex. He's definitely got that Holden Caulfield "woe-is-me, it's not my fault I'm an asshole" vibe. I was hoping this volume was just setting up something more interesting for the future issues--I understand it can take an author a little while to get their feet under them--but having read through volume six, it's mostly setup with little payoff. It does get gradually better, especially after O'Malley hires on some other artists, but not enough to make reading it worthwhile.<br /><br />The art was so-so: not bad enough to distract, not good enough to stand out. I'm all for independent B&amp;W comics, from Jhonen to Miller, Sim, Eastman and Laird, Clowes, Hernandez, Kurtzman, Crumb, and Cho but if this is all we get, I'm less than impressed.<br /><br /><b>
  <a href="http://starsbeetlesandfools.blogspot.com/2013/09/suggested-readings-in-comics.html" rel="nofollow noopener">My Suggested Reading In Comics</a>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="926929286883501851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2219758076" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2219758076" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2219758076?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=you-can-watch-it-on-the-telly">you-can-watch-it-on-the-telly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=graphic-nouvelle">graphic-nouvelle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2219758076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18226395431400194126"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>The movie adaptation of this comic book series came out during my second year of college. I went to go see it with friends and we were totally blown away because everything was so "scene" that it literally <i>hurt</i>, and also all the video game and anime callbacks, plus the fact that it was kind of like a Jackie Chan movie as done by Judd Apatow. My twenty-year-old brain was blown away by the awesome, and it never occurred to me to question t</span>
  <span id="freeText18226395431400194126" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>The movie adaptation of this comic book series came out during my second year of college. I went to go see it with friends and we were totally blown away because everything was so "scene" that it literally <i>hurt</i>, and also all the video game and anime callbacks, plus the fact that it was kind of like a Jackie Chan movie as done by Judd Apatow. My twenty-year-old brain was blown away by the awesome, and it never occurred to me to question the fact that this book puts "slacker" culture on a pedestal, features an unrepentant manchild as a protagonist, and has a twenty-three-year-old who's in a relationship with a seventeen-year-old. Ew.<br><br><br><br>My brother recently lent me this to read, since I'd never actually <i>read </i>the graphic novel, and I was pleasantly surprised by how closely the movie follows this installment at least. Twenty-eight-year-old me is far less impressed with Scott. He's actually a creep. The kind who sends creepy messages about dating on non-dating sites, talking about "connections." I didn't like how he free-loaded off his roommate, Wallace. I didn't like how he basically trashed his band's effort because he didn't want to look like he was too involved, thereby risking rejection and loss of face. I didn't like that he was dating a high school girl, and I didn't like that he cheated on said high school girl, seeming to argue that because their relationship wasn't sexual, he couldn't actually cheat on her. I didn't like how he stalked Ramona at the party, and then, when he found out where she worked and that she was the primary Amazon delivery driver in the area, <i>orders something online</i>, thereby forcing her to come to his door, and then asks her out - while she's on the clock - and not signing for the dang package until she agrees to go out with him. Scott Pilgrim is the absolute worst kind of over-entitled male, the kind that people write books about, and I was surprised at how much I could not stand him.<br><br><br><br>That said, all the other characters in this book are great. I liked the band mates. Knives Chau was cute. Ramona is cool (albeit in a manic pixie dreamgirl way). Wallace is awesome. The surreal, video game/kung-fu movie atmosphere is still present in the comic books and I liked that air of magic realism. The book, like the movie, is also so "scene" that it hurts, although since the book was published in 2004, it comes across as far more dated. For example, Scott refers to Amazon as "that book selling website." Amazon used to only sell books and CDs before becoming the mega-online retailer behemoth that they are today. There are a few other dated references like that that kind of made me smile a little, even though they feel so jarring (I'm getting old! oh noes!).<br><br><br><br>Scott is not an ideal male by any means, but the art and the story are compelling regardless. Even if you don't like Scott, the story itself is pretty cool, as is the medium in which it's told. He won't be winning Man of the Year any time soon, but I would definitely read the other books in this sceries.<br><br><br><br>3.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="18226395431400194126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1497958840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1497958840" />
    <a title="Jeannette Nikolova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2574284-jeannette-nikolova"><img alt="Jeannette Nikolova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480677087p2/2574284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1497958840?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeannette Nikolova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeannette Nikolova" href="/user/show/2574284-jeannette-nikolova">Jeannette Nikolova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1497958840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11006829899075663071"><a href='https://wondrousbooks.wordpress.com/2016/01/12/scott-pilgrims-precious-little-life-by-bryan-lee-omalley/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Read on the WondrousBooks blog.</i>
</a><br/><br/>I watched the <b>Scott Pilgrim vs. the World</b> movie years ago and it was real love. For a while it topped the “Jeannette’s Favourite Movies” list. (Even as I’m writing this, I have a strong urge to re-watch it.)<br/><br/>Therefore, it’s probably completely understandable that I absolutely loved this book. It was <b>
  <i>fan-tastic!</i>
</b> And obviously while they were making the movie, they paid huge attention to detail, because even though I had forgotten some moments and scenes, it w</span>
  <span id="freeText11006829899075663071" style="display:none"><a href="https://wondrousbooks.wordpress.com/2016/01/12/scott-pilgrims-precious-little-life-by-bryan-lee-omalley/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Read on the WondrousBooks blog.</i>
</a><br /><br />I watched the <b>Scott Pilgrim vs. the World</b> movie years ago and it was real love. For a while it topped the “Jeannette’s Favourite Movies” list. (Even as I’m writing this, I have a strong urge to re-watch it.)<br /><br />Therefore, it’s probably completely understandable that I absolutely loved this book. It was <b>
  <i>fan-tastic!</i>
</b> And obviously while they were making the movie, they paid huge attention to detail, because even though I had forgotten some moments and scenes, it was so easy to re-imagine everything in color and with the actual actors, simply because every scene was executed precisely as it was drawn.<br /><br />The story is obviously hilariously awesome, all of the characters are such weirdos, it’s so good. I loved the dry humor and the sarcastic remarks to a degree in which I felt like all of the characters are my soulmates at one point or another.<br />To be honest, out of all of them, Scott is not my favourite by far. However that might be part of the point. As well as having the readers love Ramona. Because that I did. She’s so cool. I totally feel like a Ramona sometimes, she’s the relatable hipster girl we were or tried to be in high school. (Though I don’t approve of her choice of boyfriends. Somehow.)<br /><br />I’m now really looking forward to finding the other parts of the series, since I was loaned this one. Fingers crossed.<br />(Also, I feel like I should mention that this is the second graphic novel I’ve read in my life, after Persepolis… Well, I read a Donald Duck thing when I was a kid, but come on… And anyway, I’m starting to feel a love for graphic novels. They are just too fun .)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11006829899075663071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1494475712" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1494475712?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim Ef" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim Ef" href="/user/show/24950067-jim-ef">Jim Ef</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1494475712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6975751049944780795">You know how sometimes writers want to please everyone? So they end up creating something like a genre-salad and its usually bad. Here we have the same thing but it works, it works so freaking well. First of all the art is a combination of manga and classic comics style. Now to the story. It starts like a music romance-comedy and then out of nowhere comes out a fighting scene!! Oh and I just love how his opponent drops money after he defeat him.<br/>The story is about Scott, a 23 year old boy who’s a</span>
  <span id="freeText6975751049944780795" style="display:none">You know how sometimes writers want to please everyone? So they end up creating something like a genre-salad and its usually bad. Here we have the same thing but it works, it works so freaking well. First of all the art is a combination of manga and classic comics style. Now to the story. It starts like a music romance-comedy and then out of nowhere comes out a fighting scene!! Oh and I just love how his opponent drops money after he defeat him.<br>The story is about Scott, a 23 year old boy who’s a little immature. He lives in a very small house with a guy named Wallace, they also share the same bed!! What? They don’t have the money to buy another one, they don’t even have a table. Anyways Scott personal life is going quite good too, he’s dating a 17 year old high school girl ( Knives ) and things are going pretty well.<br><br>Nothing last forever and one day Scott meets the girl of his dreams ( Ramona ), seriously he dreamed her first and then saw her in real life. Naturally he wants to meet her. They match so he wants to stop dating Knives ( but hasn't told her yet ). That’s it, they lived happily ever after……sorry they will live happily ever after if he defeats Ramona’s evil ex-boyfriends.<br><br>I’ve seen the movie ( it’s good btw ) but this is better. It knock me out<br>image: <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451997908ra/17630841.gif" width="180" height="140" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1144423854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1144423854" />
    <a title="Mehsi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6720768-mehsi"><img alt="Mehsi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588684075p2/6720768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1144423854?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mehsi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mehsi" href="/user/show/6720768-mehsi">Mehsi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=1-twinkling-star">1-twinkling-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6720768-mehsi?shelf=warning-english-books">warning-english-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144423854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14205516938862242538">Wow Scott is a real dick. Having a girlfriend and then going for another girl? Seriously? I hate that kind of attitude in books/manga/graphic novels so this is -2 stars for that. -1 star for the slightly boring story.<br/><br/>I have been meaning to read this book/comic for some time, lots of people seem to like it and I loved Bryan Lee O'Malley's previous book named: Seconds. However this was just a disappointment.<br/><br/>We have a main character named Scott Pilgrim and he is pretty useless. Lives with a friend,</span>
  <span id="freeText14205516938862242538" style="display:none">Wow Scott is a real dick. Having a girlfriend and then going for another girl? Seriously? I hate that kind of attitude in books/manga/graphic novels so this is -2 stars for that. -1 star for the slightly boring story.<br /><br />I have been meaning to read this book/comic for some time, lots of people seem to like it and I loved Bryan Lee O'Malley's previous book named: Seconds. However this was just a disappointment.<br /><br />We have a main character named Scott Pilgrim and he is pretty useless. Lives with a friend, sleeps in the same "bed", most of the stuff in said house is from the friend, and I haven't seen him do anything that might hint to work/college/or something else. It seems he sleeps, drinks, sleeps, goes out on dates with his girlfriend, sleeps, band, band and band. He seemed healthy enough to be able to work or go to college, so I am kind of wondering why he is like this.<br />Then we have his whole attitude of I-am-cool/awesome-and-the-rest-of-you-suck-or-aren't-that-awesome. Or his whole attitude regarding girls. He is dating a girl, a high-school girl at that (wth?, isn't this kind of illegal?) and while he is dating her, he is also falling for another girl named Ramona. Who apparently pops up for no reason in his dreams. He asks her to date and he even makes out/has sex with her while STILL in a relationship with his high-school girl. Dude, NO, just NO. You can't have both and you need to stop being such a dick. That High-school girl (btw, who the hell names their kid Knives) deserves better. A boyfriend worthy of her, not a dick who thinks he is so awesome and in the mean time fucks other girls.<br />Seriously I don't get why people like this kind of behaviour in books or any other media. I hate cheating, I hate dishonesty in a relationship. And like I said in the first part, I am deducting lots of points because of that.<br /><br />If that wasn't bad enough we suddenly get battle scenes in the second part???? Hold on, how did we go from: -Useless guy dates 2 girls, meanwhile has no life- to full battle mode and magics and all that? Seriously? These guys are Ramona's exes? What about the word EX do they not understand? EX-boyfriend means you aren't her boyfriend any more, and that you have no more say on with whom she goes out with. So why the battles? It is silly and it murdered the parts I liked about the book. I was so ready to drop the book when it turned out the whole second part was about him defeating Ramona's precious exes. <br />Also did he ever break up with Knives? I can't remember in my fury towards the crappy second part. <br /><br />The art was only decent. Nothing really special.<br /><br />All in all, I wouldn't recommend this book.<br /><br />Review first posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twirlingbookprincess.com/">http://twirlingbookprincess.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14205516938862242538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</p><br/><br/>Okay. So. Here’s the problem I have with this comic: I have seen it’s movie counterpart nearly 100 times. I can quote it word for word, and I loved it because it was cool to see a comic like movie.   <span id="freeText5768048457476129438" style="display:none"><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514478438ra/24781116.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><br>Okay. So. Here’s the problem I have with this comic: I have seen it’s movie counterpart nearly 100 times. I can quote it word for word, and I loved it because it was cool to see a comic like movie. With that being said, I think it may have ruined any potential enjoyment I would have gotten from this comic had I not seen the movie.<br><br>It should be pointed out that the comic basically acted as the movies script, and was nearly word for word from comic to screen. I guess I was hoping for more character development from the comic than I got with the movie. However even though they are basically the same, it’s just been further brought to my attention how much these characters actually suck as people. I could go deeper into that explanation, but I don’t want to waste anyone’s time explain how Scott is lazy, and unmotivated and how Ramona is just -meh-. <br><br>I will say if you can get your hands on one of the remastered colored versions of this comic, as the black and white original is very lackluster and toned down the whole reading experience. </span>

  <span id="freeText3299144201513450172" style="display:none">This is a black and white graphic novel about a self-absorbed 23 year old boy. There is a scene at the end where Scott has a big fight with an ex-boyfriend of his current crush that is epic. The series is set up to be Scott having to fight 7 evil ex-boyfriends for the hand of Ramona. <br /><br />He is also dating a 17 year old high schooler who he wants to break up with. I actually enjoy this series and I don't know that I like Scott all that much. I like his gay roommate Wallace better. Wallace is an asshole and he doesn't hide it. He is honest and does try and charm you. I also like Ramona. She seems cool accept she likes Scott - big minus for her.<br /><br />I thought it would be a colored graphic novel. I get bored with the black and white sometimes. The story was entertaining and I will read on. It tells a good story. </span>

<div id="review_1716944366" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1716944366" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52343138-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604747861p2/52343138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1716944366?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/52343138-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007340477" href="/book/show/7942604-scott-pilgrim-s-precious-little-life">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52343138-lauren?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1716944366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4676538384354486218">Well that was different!<br/><br/>Scott Pilgrim's Precious Little Life is a funny graphic novel to review, not because it was laugh out loud funny but because it was a bit 'meh'. <br/><br/>I have had time to reflect upon it, and having originally awarded it 4 stars, I have downgraded it to 3. There are several reasons why I have done this:<br/><br/>1) Despite O'Malley's cute illustrations, most of his characters look the same, and unless he drastically changes their hair, their facial features are mirrors of each other. Thes</span>
  <span id="freeText4676538384354486218" style="display:none">Well that was different!<br /><br />Scott Pilgrim's Precious Little Life is a funny graphic novel to review, not because it was laugh out loud funny but because it was a bit 'meh'. <br /><br />I have had time to reflect upon it, and having originally awarded it 4 stars, I have downgraded it to 3. There are several reasons why I have done this:<br /><br />1) Despite O'Malley's cute illustrations, most of his characters look the same, and unless he drastically changes their hair, their facial features are mirrors of each other. These is incredibly confusing from a reader's perspective - half the time, I had to figure out if I was following Scott or one of his friends :/<br /><br />2) I just didn't find it funny. The humour at times is kind of puerile, and I do love to entertain silliness every now and again, but I just didn't like the story. <br /><br />3) I had a huge problem with the protagonist, Scott Pilgrim. He is a very unlikeable character - conceited, heartless (where Knives Chau is concerned) and very self-important. I didn't warm to him at all and I think Knives and Ramona are better off without him.<br /><br />4) There was no real exposition - for example, Ramona's ex-boyfriends knew they had to fight Scott, but WHY? Where did this come from? Similarly, why did Scott just accept the fact that he had to fight her evil exes? IT MAKES NO SENSE!!! Why is Scott such a good fighter? Why don't we see him training, or provide some sort of back story to make sense of this? Everyone just seems to accept whatever is thrown at them and I really don't like that. You have to establish the setting/set-up early on and this really wasn't the case with SP.<br /><br />Having read Scott Pilgrim's Precious Little Life, I doubt I'm going to read any more. It left me feeling annoyed that the exposition wasn't there. I have tried reading O'Malley's stuff before (Lost at Sea) but again, I didn't really like that. He's a great artist, his characters are very cute, but he needs to differentiate between them. Also, I just don't really enjoy his storytelling. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4676538384354486218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicolo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicolo" href="/user/show/533046-nicolo">Nicolo</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer834914378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14496111752299521769">I can't believe it's been ten years since Scott Pilgrim was published and at least five since I discovered Bryan Lee O'Malley's truly original concept. <br/> <br/>I've started rereading this series earlier today and it was just as fresh as I discovered. Scott Pilgrim was this shallow guy dating high school girls and mooching off his roommate; but one could just not help root for him. Especially when he falls for the mysterious Ramona Flowers and because now he started dating her, now has to fight her seve</span>
  <span id="freeText14496111752299521769" style="display:none">I can't believe it's been ten years since Scott Pilgrim was published and at least five since I discovered Bryan Lee O'Malley's truly original concept. <br /> <br />I've started rereading this series earlier today and it was just as fresh as I discovered. Scott Pilgrim was this shallow guy dating high school girls and mooching off his roommate; but one could just not help root for him. Especially when he falls for the mysterious Ramona Flowers and because now he started dating her, now has to fight her seven exes.<br /><br />The storytelling was truly original; reading it evoked of computer games one used to play in a gaming console. In fact, fighting Ramona's exes in succession reminded me of boss fights in Final Fantasy or any other similar role playing game. A vanquished disappearing in a pile of coins completed the video game conceit.<br /><br />Video games were not the only pop culture O'Malley drew on. Comics were constantly referred and it appears that the author was great fan of the X-Men.<br /><br />It will be great to read this series again. Although I may no longer the original feeling when I first discovered this book, it is close enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14496111752299521769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2263343453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2263343453" />
    <a title="Brian Yahn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22849115-brian-yahn"><img alt="Brian Yahn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464719293p2/22849115.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2263343453?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Yahn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Yahn" href="/user/show/22849115-brian-yahn">Brian Yahn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2263343453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5071054129690556147">Everything about Scott Pilgrim is fun.<br/><br/>There's a feel to it. It's in the mood. The illustrations give the world this video-game vibe. And the premise seems like something out straight out of a video game.<br/><br/>Scott Pilgram has to defeat his love interest's seven evil-ex boyfriends. In this book, we only meet one evil-ex, but the way Scott defeats him, through song, is incredibly fun.<br/><br/>But even with everything the series had going for it, I'm not sure I'll continue. In the first installment, I wanted to </span>
  <span id="freeText5071054129690556147" style="display:none">Everything about Scott Pilgrim is fun.<br /><br />There's a feel to it. It's in the mood. The illustrations give the world this video-game vibe. And the premise seems like something out straight out of a video game.<br /><br />Scott Pilgram has to defeat his love interest's seven evil-ex boyfriends. In this book, we only meet one evil-ex, but the way Scott defeats him, through song, is incredibly fun.<br /><br />But even with everything the series had going for it, I'm not sure I'll continue. In the first installment, I wanted to see more depth from the characters. There's some questions left unanswered, but nothing major was revealed about any of them that really piqued my interest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5071054129690556147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
